I had picked a car but unfortunately it got sold before I had the money. So, I found another one, even a few grand cheaper. So, I finally got paid and take several different forms of transportation to get there(  I live in San Diego). Once the deal starts they inform me that because of the financing they have to use for me ( I have bad credit) there are all of these extra charges this particular finance company requires, it made my nice $6,000 vehicle go up to almost $9,000. On top of that the finance charge is 28%. I knew that the APR would be that high but I didn‚Äôt expect them to include almost $4,000. So now my vehicle is going to cost me almost $20 grand when it‚Äôs paid off in 4 years!!! I almost left and forgot about doing the deal but I needed a car so bad!! So, they were very nice and helpful but I definitely got taken to the cleaners!! Just be aware when buying from them....</text>

So the rest are considered "vintage" but even the newer manual lenses(some of which are in production today) are considered "worthless" to pawn shops. I shoot manual and value the mechanical fortitude and high quality glass that lenses used to have, and I know I'm not alone with a huge resurgence in popularity due to mirrorless cameras. This was one of the few shops that even gave me an offer - for starters my crown jewel is my SMC/Super Takumar(aka Pentax) collection: f3.5:28mm, f2:35mm, f3.5:35mm, f1.4:50mm, auto f2:55mm, f2:55mm, f1.8:55mm, f1.9:85mm, f3.5:135mm, f4:200mm and if anyone knows anything about these its that they sell easy due to their high build & image quality. Same with Nikkor, same with Zeiss, same with Meyer-Optik - they're all legendary and sell easily, so not worthless. I had to of had 20 lenses that would easily sell for $100 and then a lens like an 85mm f1.9 or 35mm f2? Closer to $200-300. Screw mount Super Takumar's were made in the 60s and 70s. <pictures>None<//pictures><user>108852700119574832643</user><user_name>Melissa Gardner</user_name><rating>5<//rating>< text>
Dr. Faisal saved my life. Not literally but just as profoundly. I had been diagnosed 2 years prior to becoming a patient of his. In that time, my insurance refused to cover the cost of a specialist and sent me around to other neurologists. Every single one of them said, they don't specialize in my diagnosis, I'm too severe, they don't know beyond the basic treatment protocol for my diagnosis and I needed to see someone specialized.
I spent years struggling, being beaten down by an insurance company who thought I'd give up. I nearly did. I nearly gave up the fight and went to live with my family and stop taking the minimally effective medicine.
When I first saw Dr. Faisal, he KNEW about my diagnosis. This was a first for me! He knew less common treatment methods and the hell I was living in. He took a great deal of time with me and came up with a plan WITH me! When I got my brain scan, he asked me to come around the other side of the screen to look at it with him.

Beyond that, his office staff are literal angels. They never stopped pushing my insurance company even after multiple denials. I don't know where they get the patience but I cannot express my gratitude enough. I have left here crying tears of joy on multiple occasions. I have my life back. My diagnosis does not dictate every thing I do anymore.
Keep in mind - because he spends individual time with you, you may wait in the waiting room longer than other doctors. Just deal with it because Dr. Faisal will give you the same attention he's giving someone else while you're waiting. Bring a book.
Also, he's still a doctor, and while I think he's the best I've ever been to, he still has all the typical doctor pragmatics, i.e., doesn't make a lot of eye contact, will cut you off mid-sentence, minimal small talk. These don't mean he doesn't care, it just means he's a doctor and spent years specializing in neurology while other people were honing their social skills (like every other neurologist).

I hesitate to write this because it will make his waitlist longer, but other people deserve the same level of medical care. So here you go :)< /text>
